He writes in characters too grand -
For our short sight to understand;
We catch but broken strokes, and try
To fathom all the mystery
Of withered hopes, of death, of life,
The endless war, the useless strife—
But there, with larger, clearer sight,
We shall see this—His way was right.
So —Ho for the Pilot's orders,
Whatever course He makes !
For He sees beyond the skyline,
And He never makes mistakes
—John Oxenham.
Ballarat Litho. & Printing Co.,


The Avenue of Honor, 1937.
[Dedicated to the patriotic young ladies of
Lucas & Co.'s, 1917.]
For this thou shalt from all things seek
Marrow of mirth and laughter,"
And wheresoe'er thou move good luck
Shall throw her old shoes after.
—Tennyson.
One evening as I wandered forth
With weary steps and slow,
Methought I saw the Lucas girls
Of twenty years ago.
I pictured them in happy homes
Where love and truth abide;
Two virtues that will smooth our path
Across the Great Divide.
The magpies carolled forth their lays,
A skylark specked the blue,
While summer birds came skimming down
The long green Avenue.
I sat me down beneath a tree,
And thought with honest pride:
These grow for Austral's fighting men
Who for our freedom died.
Two blackbirds whistled overhead,
Their notes of music true;
I blessed the tender, lloyal hearts
That planned the Avenue.
More fitting than a monument
In sculptured figures dres't;
These trees are live memorials
Of those we love th<e best.
The men who placed ttheir country first,
And gave what goldl can't buy,
While human pangs and passions last,
Their names shall never die.
The sword is rusted in sheath,
Farms dot the battle plain,
And Peace triumphant sits enthroned
Above the noble slain.
Warmed by the breath of blue-eyed spring,
The trees in beauty grow,
A credit to the Lucas girls
Of twenty years ago.
—JAMES BARBOUR,
Melrose Estate, Victoria

INDIVIDUAL TREE.


For First Planting, June 4th, 1917, and
subsequent Plantings.
The enclosed list of names of soldiers from the Beautiful
City of Ballarat who have offered their services to our beloved
Empire for active service abroad, and in whose honour we
are planting an Avenue of Trees is as near perfect in the order
of their • enlistjnent as it has been possible to procure the
information. They have been listed. in the same order as
they appear on the Military Rolls at the Base Records Office '
on the day of enlistment.
It will be noted that only a few of the names show the
rank to which the soldier has risen. This appears only against
the ones that have either been killed or discharged; also the
mark denoting those who' have made the supreme sacrifice.
This will be added to the other plates, along with the rank,
as the information is available. If the next of kin will kindly
post the information to us, we will arrange to have it written
on the name plate at an early date.
Yours respectfully
SCttcaiT
The following list will serve to indicate the kind of
tree that has been planted for each soldier:—
